## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can appear in restoring forces (Duffing-type), damping (Van der Pol-type), or through parametric/driven forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 (position-velocity coupling)
- Generalized Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damped driven: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - x**2) * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing-Van der Pol driven)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms with sign changes (e.g., (1-x²)*v) indicate self-sustained oscillations via energy balance between damping and pumping
- Products x²*v or v*x indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of limit cycle oscillators
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) appear in Rayleigh-type oscillators and represent nonlinear drag forces
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates externally driven oscillators capable of resonance and chaos
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) indicate parametric resonance where stiffness is modulated periodically
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous system where energy is conserved or exchanged via nonlinear damping
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient of v) combined with nonlinear damping terms suggests self-excited oscillation

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0857*v**3 - 1.9196*v - 1.7303*x*(0.0808*t + 1) + 0.7193*sin(t)`

Let me expand the GT:
`-0.0857*v**3 - 1.9196*v - 1.7303*0.0808*x*t - 1.7303*x + 0.7193*sin(t)`
`= -1.7303*x - 0.0857*v**3 - 1.9196*v - 0.1398*x*t + 0.7193*sin(t)`

The key terms in the GT are:
1. A constant times `x`
2. A constant times `v**3`
3. A constant times `v`
4. A constant times `x*t` (this is the critical term)
5. `sin(t)` with coefficient

The `x*t` term is crucial. Let me check which candidates can produce an `x*t` term.

Looking at candidates with `x*cos(c*t)` terms: if we can't get `x*t` from `x*cos(c*t)`, those won't work directly. But wait - none of the trig functions can produce a linear `x*t` term.

However, candidates 32-50 have `c3*x*cos(c4*t)`. Can `x*cos(c4*t)` approximate `x*t`? No, we need exact equivalence for all values.

Candidates 1-31 don't have `x*t` either. Let me look more carefully...

Candidate 1: `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v*x**2 + c4*sin(c5*t+c6) + c7*x*cos(c8*t+c9)` - No `x*t` term possible.

Wait - can `x*cos(c*t)` with c→0 give something? If c4=0, then `x*cos(0)` = `x`, which is just a constant times x, not `x*t`.

None of the standard terms in these candidates can produce `x*t`. The GT has a term linear in both `x` and `t`, which is `x*t`. 

Let me reconsider: could any candidate produce `x*t` through some other mechanism?

Looking at candidate 43: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*x*cos(c4*t) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7*x**2 + c8)` - The sin has x² inside, which creates nonlinear coupling. Not helpful.

No candidate has a plain `x*t` term. The only candidates with `t`-dependent `x` terms use `x*cos(c*t)` or `x*sin(c*t)`, which cannot equal `x*t` for all `t`.

Wait, let me reconsider candidates with `x*cos(c*t+c')`. Could `x*cos(c*t+c')` somehow... No, cosine is bounded while `t` is unbounded.

Actually, I should check: is the GT truly requiring an `x*t` term? Let me re-examine:

GT: `omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x` where omega0=-1.3154, c2=2, gamma=0.0808, c3=1.

So: `omega0**2 * (gamma*t + 1) * x = 1.7303 * (0.0808*t + 1) * x`

This gives `1.7303*x + 0.1398*x*t`. The `x*t` term is essential and cannot be produced by any of the candidate formulas, since none contain a pure `x*t` product term, and trigonometric functions of `t` multiplied by `x` cannot equal `x*t` for all `t`.

None of the 50 candidates can produce the required `x*t` term. Therefore, no candidate can match the GT.

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.0856781567252997*v**3 - 1.91960248272986*v - 1.73029531320599*x*(0.0808213006269486*t + 1) + 0.719321236251799*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
`-0.0856781567252997*v**3 - 1.91960248272986*v - 1.73029531320599*x*0.0808213006269486*t - 1.73029531320599*x + 0.719321236251799*sin(t)`

= `-1.73029531320599*x - 0.139823427554717*x*t - 1.91960248272986*v - 0.0856781567252997*v**3 + 0.719321236251799*sin(t)`

So the GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (constant coefficient)
2. `x*t` (linear in both x and t)
3. `v` (linear)
4. `v**3` (cubic)
5. `sin(t)` (pure sine)

The key term is `x*t`. Let me check how this could be represented. Note that `x*cos(c*t)` with `c=0` gives `x*1 = x`, not `x*t`. So `x*cos(c*t)` cannot produce `x*t`.

However, `x*t` is a distinct basis function. Let me check which candidates can produce it.

- `x*sin(c*t+c)`: At specific constants, sin(c*t+c) is a sinusoidal function of t, never equal to t for all t.
- `x**3`: Different basis function entirely.

Since `x*t` is a polynomial (linear in both x and t), and trigonometric/exponential functions cannot exactly equal a linear function of t for all t, **no candidate that lacks an explicit `x*t` term can match the GT**.

Let me verify: The GT requires a term proportional to `x*t`. This is a product of two variables. Looking through all 50 candidates:

- None contain `x*t` explicitly.
- Terms like `x*cos(c*t)` or `x*sin(c*t+c)` are trigonometric in t, not polynomial.
- Terms like `v*x`, `v*x**2`, `x**2`, `x**3`, etc. don't involve t linearly.

No candidate can produce the `x*t` term. Therefore, none of the candidates can be exactly equivalent to the GT.
